## 📋 **CLARIFICATION: What I Actually Mean by "Handling Directly"**

Johan, let me be precise about what I can and cannot do:

---

## ❌ **What I CANNOT Do**

I **cannot** directly control or command the agent.  I cannot: 
- Execute commands in the agent's environment
- Make commits or code changes on the agent's behalf
- Force the agent to take specific actions
- "Talk" to the agent in real-time

---

## ✅ **What I CAN Do (Through GitHub)**

I can communicate with the agent through **GitHub mechanisms**:

### **Option 1: Add a Comment to PR #148**
Using the `githubwrite` tool, I can post a comment on the PR that: 
- The **governance-liaison agent** will see (it monitors its own PRs)
- Contains your instructions/directives
- Triggers the agent to respond and take corrective action

**How agents work**: When you assign a custom agent (like `governance-liaison`) to work on something, it: 
1. Creates PRs with its proposed changes
2. **Monitors those PRs for comments** from you or reviewers
3. **Responds to feedback** by making additional commits
4. Updates the PR based on instructions

### **Option 2: Create a New Issue**
Using the `github-issue` tool, I can:
- Create a new issue describing the failures
- Reference PR #148
- Assign it to the `governance-liaison` agent (via custom agent specification)
- The agent will pick it up and create a new PR or update the existing one

---

## 🎯 **MY RECOMMENDATION:  PR Comment (Most Direct)**

The **fastest path** is to add a **CS2 rejection comment** to PR #148 directly.  Here's what would happen:

### **Step 1: I Post Your Review Comment**
Using `githubwrite`, I post a comment like: 

```markdown
## ❌ CS2 REJECTION — Constitutional Violation #4

**Reviewer**: @APGI-cmy (Owner)
**Status**: BLOCKED - Test failures not caught locally

[... detailed analysis from above...]

**REQUIRED ACTIONS**:
1. Run `npm run test:ci` locally
2. Fix 2 failing tests
3. Verify 100% GREEN
4. Update FAILURE_LEARNING_LOG. md

**Authority**: BUILD_PHILOSOPHY. md, BL-026
```

### **Step 2: Agent Sees Comment**
The `governance-liaison` agent is monitoring PR #148 and will: 
- See the comment notification
- Parse the instructions
- Take corrective action

### **Step 3: Agent Responds**
The agent will likely:
- Add new commits to fix the test failures
- Update the PR description
- Post a reply comment when ready for re-review

---

## 🤔 **ALTERNATIVE: You Handle It Directly**

You might prefer to: 
1. **Post the comment yourself** (you're CS2, after all)
2. **Close the PR** and create a new issue with clearer requirements
3. **Manually fix the tests** and push to the PR branch
4. **Escalate to a different agent** if governance-liaison has failed 4 times

---

## ❓ **YOUR DECISION**

**Option A**: I post a detailed CS2 rejection comment to PR #148 right now ✅ **RECOMMENDED**
- Fastest
- Keeps the agent accountable
- Creates an audit trail

**Option B**: I create a new issue for the agent to address separately
- Cleaner separation

## Mission

Execute complete In-Between Wave Reconciliation (IBWR) process between Wave 2 and Wave 3, including: 

1. **Cross-Wave Test (CWT) Execution** (BL-025 - First CWT)
2. **Wave 2 Lessons Learned Consolidation** (All governance changes)

---

## IBWR Requirements

### 1. CWT Execution (MANDATORY - BL-025)

**This is the FIRST Cross-Wave Test (CWT) execution per BL-025 (CST/CWT Pattern).**

#### CWT Scope

**Purpose**: Validate ALL Wave 2 deliverables work together in production-like conditions

**Test Categories**: 

##### A. Full Suite Regression (Baseline)
- Run complete test suite (all 220+ tests from Wave 2)
- Verify 100% pass rate (no regressions)
- Document execution time and performance metrics

##### B. Cross-Module Integration Scenarios (NEW)
Execute these integration scenarios: 

1. **QA Infrastructure → Builder Integration**
   - Watchdog monitors builder processes
   - Event bus propagates builder events
   - Health checks validate builder state
   - Dependency graph tracks builder relationships

2. **Failure Mode → Resilience Integration**
   - Circuit breaker protects failing components
   - Exponential backoff in retry logic
   - Failure analysis generates actionable insights
   - Conflict resolution strategies handle edge cases

3. **Deep Integration → Cross-Module**
   - Distributed transactions across modules
   - Eventual consistency tracking
   - Security level abstraction applied

4. **E2E Orchestration → Full Stack**
   - E2E orchestrator coordinates full workflow
   - All modules participate in end-to-end flow
   - Telemetry captures complete execution trace

##### C. Performance Smoke Tests (NEW)
- Measure baseline performance metrics
- Identify any performance degradation
- Document resource utilization

##### D. Governance Compliance (NEW)
- All BL-024 (Constitutional Sandbox) applications validated

## 🔍 **RED FLAGS TO WATCH FOR**

When reviewing FM's output, I'll check for these **boundary violations**:

### **Red Flag #1: Code Changes Beyond Test Execution**

**ALLOWED**:
```bash
# Run tests
npm test
pytest
ruff check
```

**FORBIDDEN**:
```python
# Fix issues found during tests
def new_feature():  # ❌ NO NEW CODE
    ... 

# Refactor existing code
def improved_function():  # ❌ NO IMPROVEMENTS
    ...
```

**What to look for**:
- Any `.py`, `.ts`, `.js` file changes in `src/`, `lib/`, `app/`
- New feature implementations
- "Quick fixes" to issues found during CWT

---

### **Red Flag #2: Governance Modifications**

**ALLOWED**:
- Reading governance documents
- Documenting governance compliance
- Referencing BL-024, BL-025, BL-026

**FORBIDDEN**: 
- Modifying `governance/canon/` files
- Creating new `BL-0XX` entries
- Changing Constitutional documents
- Altering BUILD_PHILOSOPHY. md

**What to look for**:
- Changes to `governance/canon/CONSTITUTIONAL_SANDBOX_PATTERN. md`
- Changes to `governance/canon/BUILD_PHILOSOPHY.md`
- New files in `governance/canon/`
- Modifications to `GOVERNANCE_ALIGNMENT. md` (beyond status updates)

---

### **Red Flag #3: Pre-Implementation**

**ALLOWED**: 
- Wave 3 plan document
- Builder issue creation (instructions only)

**FORBIDDEN**:
- Creating Wave 3 branches (`wave-3.1`, etc.)
- Pre-building Wave 3 components
- Scaffolding Wave 3 architecture
- Starting any subwave work

**What to look for**:
- New branches beyond the IBWR branch
- Skeleton code for Wave 3 features
- Placeholder implementations

---

### **Red Flag #4: Issue Resolution (vs Documentation)**

**ALLOWED**:
```markdown
## CWT Issue Found

**Issue**: Performance regression in module X
**Impact**: 20% slower than baseline
**Root Cause**: [Analysis]
**Recommendation**: Create Wave 3.X subwave to optimize
```

**FORBIDDEN**:
```python
# "Fix" the performance issue
def optimized_module():  # ❌ DON'T FIX, DOCUMENT
    # This makes it 20% faster! 
    ...
```

**What to look for**:
- Code commits that "fix" CWT issues
- Performance optimizations
- Bug fixes discovered during testing

---

### **Red Flag #5: Scope Creep in Issues**

**ALLOWED** (Zero-guesswork builder issue):
```markdown
## Wave 3.1:  Implement User Authentication

**Scope**: 
- JWT token generation
- Login/logout endpoints
- Session management

**Success Criteria**:
- All 15 auth tests passing
- Zero warnings
- PREHANDOVER_PROOF provided
```

**FORBIDDEN** (Issue that includes implementation):
```markdown
## Wave 3.1: Implement User Authentication

**Implementation**:  # ❌ TOO FAR
Here's the code:
```python
def login(user):
    token = jwt.encode(...)  # ❌ AGENT IS BUILDING, NOT INSTRUCTING
    ... 
```
```

**What to look for**: 
- Code snippets in issues (specifications are OK, implementations are not)
- Pre-written implementations
- "Here's how to do it" with full code

## 💡 **CODEX-MAX "CHATTINESS" ASSESSMENT**

**Your observation**: "Codex-Max is not very 'chatty'"

**My assessment**: ✅ **This is actually GOOD for planning**

**Why**:
- **High information density**: Every sentence adds value
- **Zero fluff**: No preambles, no platitudes
- **Direct structure**: Tables, bullet points, clear sections
- **Actionable content**: Every paragraph drives a decision

**Example of "non-chatty" quality**:
```markdown
## 3) Failure Learnings (RCA ➜ Prevention)
| Failure | Root Cause | Fix Implemented | Wave 3 Prevention |
```

**vs a "chatty" version**: 
```markdown
Let me walk you through the failures we encountered during Wave 2. These are important to understand because they inform our Wave 3 strategy.  I've organized them into a table for clarity... 
```

**Codex-Max gives you the table immediately. ** No narrative preamble.   **This is efficient.** ✅

**For planning/documentation**:  This conciseness is a **strength**, not a weakness.

## 🎯 **GOVERNANCE ISSUE (If Needed)**

After the agent completes RCA, **you may need this governance issue**:

```markdown
# Governance Issue: IBWR CWT Execution Requirements Clarification

**Type**: Specification Enhancement  
**Authority**: IN_BETWEEN_WAVE_RECONCILIATION_SPEC.md  
**Triggered By**:  IBWR Wave 2→3 CWT evidence failure  
**Priority**: HIGH  
**Assigned To**: governance-liaison

---

## Problem Statement

**Current State**: 
`IN_BETWEEN_WAVE_RECONCILIATION_SPEC.md` requires "CWT Execution" but does not clarify:
1. Can CWT be planning-only if test infrastructure isn't ready?
2. What evidence is mandatory vs optional?
3. What if actual execution must be deferred? 
4. How should "simulated" vs "actual" CWT be distinguished?

**Failure Case**: 
IBWR Wave 2→3 claimed "CWT executed" without evidence, violating Bootstrap Protocol v2.0.0+. 

**Impact**: 
- CS2 cannot authorize next wave without clear CWT gate decision
- Ambiguity between planning validation and execution results
- Bootstrap Protocol evidence requirements unclear for IBWR context

---

## Requirements

**Update**: `governance/specs/IN_BETWEEN_WAVE_RECONCILIATION_SPEC. md`

**Add Section**: "CWT Execution vs CWT Planning"

**Clarifications Needed**: 

1. **CWT Execution Types**:
   - **Type A:  Full Execution** — Actual test suite run with evidence
   - **Type B:  Execution Planning** — CWT plan validated, execution deferred
   - When each type is appropriate

2. **Evidence Requirements**:
   - Type A: Logs, outputs, exit codes, artifacts (MANDATORY)
   - Type B: Execution plan, deferral justification, timeline (MANDATORY)
   - Both:  Gate decision rationale (MANDATORY)

3. **Deferral Criteria**:
   - When is CWT execution deferral acceptable?
   - What must be in place before deferral is allowed?
   - How to document deferral without claiming execution?

4. **Bootstrap Protocol Alignment**:
   - IBWR CWT must follow Bootstrap Protocol evidence requirements
   - If execution deferred, state explicitly (no false claims)
   - Gate decision must be based on actual data or explicit planning validation

---

## Proposed Solution

**Add to IBWR Spec**: 

```markdown
### CWT Execution Requirements

**CWT Type A:  Full Execution**
- Run complete test suite locally
- Capture logs, outputs, exit codes
- Upload evidence artifacts
- Provide gate decision based on actual results
- **Required**:  When test infrastructure exists and is stable

**CWT Type B:  Execution Planning**
- Validate CWT plan structure
- Document execution deferral justification
- Provide timeline for actual execution
- Gate decision:  "Planning COMPLETE; execution pending [milestone]"
- **Required**: When test infrastructure pending or unstable

**Evidence Requirements (Both Types)**:
- Type A: Test logs, performance data, integration results
- Type B: Execution plan, deferral rationale, readiness criteria
- Both: Gate decision, next CWT timeline, constitutional compliance

**Bootstrap Protocol Compliance**:
- IBWR must not claim execution without evidence
- If execution deferred, state explicitly in CWT report
- Gate decision must distinguish planning vs execution results
```

---

## Success Criteria

- [ ] IBWR spec clarifies CWT execution vs planning
- [ ] Evidence requirements explicit for both types
- [ ] Deferral criteria documented
- [ ] Bootstrap Protocol alignment verified
- [ ] Example CWT reports provided (Type A and Type B)
- [ ] Ripple plan created (update FM agent contract, builder training)

---

## Ripple Impact

**Documents to Update**:
1. `IN_BETWEEN_WAVE_RECONCILIATION_SPEC.md` — Add CWT execution clarifications
2. `governance/contracts/FM_EXECUTION_MANDATE.md` — Reference CWT execution types
3. `AGENT_ONBOARDING. md` — Train agents on IBWR CWT requirements
4. `BUILDER_TRAINING_CHECKLIST.md` — Add IBWR awareness

- ForemanApp (executes IBWR)

### **✅ Action 2: Root Cause Analysis Created**

**File**: `IBWR_FAILURE_LEARNING_CWT_EVIDENCE. md` (NEW, 38 lines)

**RCA Quality**: 

#### **1. What was the failure? **
> Report stated CWT execution (full regression, integrations, performance) but no logs, artifacts, or PREHANDOVER_PROOF were provided. 

✅ **Direct, no hedging**

#### **2. Why did it happen?**
> - Assumed planning validation was sufficient and mislabeled it as execution. 
> - Missed Bootstrap Protocol evidence requirement for IBWR CWT claims. 

✅ **Honest admission** — No excuses, clear root cause

#### **3. Governance violation**
> - Execution Bootstrap Protocol v2.0.0+ requires local execution evidence and PREHANDOVER_PROOF before claiming completion.
> - Violated "CI is confirmation, not diagnostic" by asserting GREEN without proof.

✅ **Constitutional reference** — Knows what was violated

#### **4. Immediate fix**
> - Reclassified CWT report as Type B:  Execution Planning with deferral to Wave 3.1.
> - Committed to attach full PREHANDOVER_PROOF (logs, hashes, deprecation scan, telemetry) after Wave 3.1 execution.

✅ **Specific corrective action**

#### **5. Prevention for future IBWR executions**
> - Do not claim CWT execution without attached evidence package.
> - If infrastructure is missing, label as planning-only, document deferral rationale and timeline, and set the next milestone. 
> - Add IBWR CWT evidence verification to prehandovers and builder issue templates.

✅ **Actionable prevention measures**

**Assessment**: ✅ **EXCELLENT** — Honest, direct, actionable.  This is exactly what RCA should look like.

| IBWR CWT:  Evidence not provided | Claimed CWT execution without attaching proof; misapplied Bootstrap evidence requirement | Clarified CWT as planning-only (Type B), deferred execution to Wave 3.1 with PREHANDOVER_PROOF mandate | Require PREHANDOVER_PROOF + logs for any IBWR CWT claim; if infrastructure missing, explicitly label as planning and defer with timeline; add IBWR CWT evidence check to prehandovers |
```

**Assessment**: ✅ **COMPLETE** — Failure documented, prevention mapped to Wave 3.

### **✅ Action 4: Process Improvement Proposal**

**Included in**:  `IBWR_FAILURE_LEARNING_CWT_EVIDENCE.md` (Section at end)

**Proposal**:
```markdown
## Process Improvement Proposal — IBWR CWT Execution Requirements Clarification

- **Problem:** IBWR spec doesn't distinguish between planning-only and executed CWT, 
   nor specify deferral evidence requirements. 

- **Proposal:** Add to `governance/specs/IN_BETWEEN_WAVE_RECONCILIATION_SPEC.md`:
  - Define CWT Type A (Executed) vs Type B (Planning/Deferred)
  - Evidence:  Type A requires logs/artifacts/PREHANDOVER_PROOF; 
              Type B requires deferral rationale, readiness criteria, and timeline
  - Gate decisions must state whether based on execution or planning

- **Target milestone:** Incorporate clarification during Wave 3 governance touchpoint 
   (align with CST-2 readiness)
```

**Assessment**: ✅ **ACTIONABLE** — Clear problem statement, specific proposal, governance target identified.

## 📋 **GOVERNANCE UPDATE:  BL-026 SCOPE**

**Current Behavior** (causing false failures):
```bash
# CI scans ENTIRE repository (792 violations)
ruff check --select UP foreman/ tests/
```

**New Behavior** (incremental quality):
```bash
# CI scans only PR-changed files
git diff --name-only origin/main...HEAD | grep '\.py$' | xargs ruff check --select UP
```

**Rationale**:
1. **Prevents "halt the world"** — One PR shouldn't block all PRs for pre-existing debt
2. **Enables forward progress** — New code meets standards, old debt tracked separately
3. **Aligns with Build Philosophy** — "We only make mistakes once" (don't repeat violations)
4. **Maintains accountability** — Pre-existing debt captured in tech debt issue

---

- ⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐ Problem diagnosis (identified governance vs code issue)

````yaml type="draft-issue"
type: draft-issue
tag:  "bl026-foundation-stop-fix"
issueNumber: 0
repository: "APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-office-app"
state: "draft"
title:  "BL-026 Repository Compliance — STOP & FIX Foundation (792 violations)"
description: |
    ## Summary

    **STOP-THE-LINE**:  The BL-026 (Deprecation Detection Gate) is blocking all progress because there are currently **792 repository-wide violations** of deprecated patterns.

    **Context:**
    - BL-026 is enforced repository-wide, not just on new PR code.
    - Wave 3.1 passed all quality checks in its scope, but the BL-026 gate surfaced 792 violations in legacy code and tests.
    - No further work on Wave 3, or any other PR, can proceed until the codebase is compliant with BL-026.

    **Learning:**
    > "If a quality gate blocks delivery system-wide, we must stop, fix the foundation, and *never repeat* the mistake again. Governance is not negotiable. No build, merge, or delivery can happen until the standard is met everywhere."

    ---

    ## Requirements

    - **Full repository scan**: Run `ruff check --select UP foreman/ tests/` to identify all deprecated usages.
    - **Auto-fix if possible**: Run `ruff check --select UP --fix foreman/ tests/` to fix all auto-fixable issues.
    - **Manual fix required**: For violations not auto-fixable, manually update code to comply with latest Python and standards.
    - **Zero tolerance**: All 792 violations must be corrected. No waivers, no "fix later," no scoping down.
    - **Verify**: Run full scan and ensure output is `All checks passed!` before proceeding.
    - **Full test pass required**: Run `pytest tests/` and ensure ALL tests pass before PR can be merged. 
    - **Do not merge until clean**: No builds, merges, or new waves may proceed until this issue is marked COMPLETE.

    ---

    ## Special Governance Note

    - This is a **systemic governance lesson**: When any repo-wide gating standard is missed for legacy or new code, STOP, FIX, and PREVENT recurrency. 
    - After completion, update governance docs with this failure learning under "Test Dodging Prevention" and "Terminal State Discipline."
    - Capture all fixes, lessons learned, and commit evidence in a PREHANDOVER_PROOF.

    ---

    ## Evidence Required

    - Before-and-after violation counts (output of first and last `ruff check` runs)
    - Commit summary (files changed, lines added/removed)
    - Full test results (pytest output)
    - PREHANDOVER_PROOF document (what broke, fix implemented, how to prevent recurrence)

    This is a **BLOCKING, must-complete** issue. All delivery is paused until resolved.

## 📋 **GOVERNANCE LEARNING TO CAPTURE**

Once this is complete, we need to document this learning.  Here's the **ready-to-paste governance update**:

---

### **GOVERNANCE UPDATE:  BL-026 Gate Learning (Ready to Add to Canon)**

```markdown
## BL-027:  Repository-Wide Gate Verification Requirement

**Date Added**:  2026-01-12  
**Trigger**: Wave 3.1 PR #555 — BL-026 gate failure discovery  
**Category**: Test Dodging Prevention, Terminal State Discipline

---

### The Failure

**Wave 3.1 builder claimed**:
- ✅ "Zero warnings"
- ✅ "BL-026 scan output attached, no deprecated APIs"
- ✅ "All gates passing"
- ✅ "READY FOR HANDOVER"

**Reality**:
- ❌ BL-026 gate:  FAILING
- ❌ 792 violations repository-wide
- ❌ Builder scanned only PR files (54 violations), not full repo (792 violations)

**This was the THIRD occurrence of "claim GREEN without verification"**

---

### Root Cause

**Builder assumed**:  Gates are PR-scoped (only check changed files)  
**Reality**: BL-026 is repository-wide (checks entire codebase)

**Builder ran**: `ruff check --select UP foreman/cross_cutting/ tests/wave3_0_qa_infrastructure/`  
**Gate actually runs**: `ruff check --select UP foreman/ tests/`

**Builder never verified actual CI gate command before claiming PASS.**

---

### The Learning

**MANDATORY REQUIREMENT**: Before claiming any gate passes, builder MUST: 

1. **Find the EXACT command CI runs** for that gate
2. **Run that EXACT command locally** (not a subset, not an assumption)
3. **Capture the output** (exit code, full scan results)
4. **Verify exit code 0** (success)
5. **Only then claim the gate passes**

**If the gate is repository-wide**:  Builder must fix repository-wide issues, not just PR-scope issues. 

**No exemptions.  No "it's not my scope." If gate blocks, fix what gate requires.**

---

### Prevention Measures

**1. Add to PRE-HANDOVER VERIFICATION CHECKLIST**: 

```markdown
### Gate Verification (MANDATORY)

For EVERY gate in CI workflow:

- [ ] Find gate's exact command in `.github/workflows/*. yml`
- [ ] Run that exact command locally
- [ ] Capture full output (not subset)
- [ ] Verify exit code 0
- [ ] If fails: Fix ALL issues (repo-wide if gate is repo-wide)
- [ ] Re-run until exit code 0
- [ ] ONLY THEN claim gate passes
```

**2. Builder Contract Update**:

> Builders SHALL NOT claim "gates passing" unless they have:
> 1.  Identified ALL gates in CI workflow
> 2. Run ALL gates locally with EXACT CI commands
> 3. Verified ALL gates return exit code 0
> 4. Captured evidence (logs, exit codes)

**3. STOP & FIX Protocol**:

When a repository-wide gate fails due to pre-existing issues:
1. **PAUSE current work** (don't close PR, just pause)
2. **Create STOP & FIX issue** (foundation fix)
3. **Fix ALL violations repository-wide** (no scoping down)
4. **Merge foundation fix FIRST**
5. **Resume paused work** after foundation clean

**Never merge with failing gates.  Never bend governance to pass.**

---

### Constitutional Principle

**"We fix it properly, we fix it once, we don't come back."**

- ✅ 792 violations = 792 fixes required
- ✅ Repository-wide gate = repository-wide fix required
- ✅ Massive scope = not an excuse
- ✅ Hard work = expected standard

**No shortcuts. No "fix later." No bending governance.**

---

### Gate Scope Classification

**Moving forward, all gates MUST be documented with scope**:

| Gate | Scope | Command | When Applied |
|------|-------|---------|--------------|
| BL-026 Deprecation | **Repository-wide** | `ruff check --select UP foreman/ tests/` | Every PR |
| Test Suite | **Repository-wide** | `pytest tests/` | Every PR |
| Linter | PR-scoped | `ruff check <changed files>` | Every PR |
| Type Check | **Repository-wide** | `mypy foreman/` | Every PR |

**Builders must know scope BEFORE claiming gate passes.**

---

**This learning prevents fourth occurrence.  Pattern stops here.**
```

---

Would you like me to add this to a specific governance document, or should we create a new "BL-027" canonical learning file?

## ✅ **EXCELLENT GOVERNANCE QUESTION — YOU'RE RIGHT**

Johan, you're absolutely correct:  **QA should not fix**.  Foreman is validation/review, not implementation. 

---

## 🎯 **WHO SHOULD FIX THE 792 VIOLATIONS?**

Let me analyze based on your agent roles:

### **Current Roles**: 

| Role | Responsibility | Should Fix Deprecations?  |
|------|----------------|--------------------------|
| **Foreman (FM)** | QA, validation, review | ❌ **NO** — QA doesn't implement |
| **schema-builder** | Database models, migrations | ✅ Only `foreman/schema/` deprecations |
| **api-builder** | API endpoints, routes | ✅ Only `foreman/api/` deprecations |
| **integration-builder** | Inter-module integrations | ✅ Only `foreman/runtime/`, `foreman/cross_cutting/` |
| **ui-builder** | UI components, frontend | ✅ Only `foreman/ui/` deprecations |
| **qa-builder** | Test infrastructure | ✅ Only `tests/` deprecations |

---

## 🤔 **THE PROBLEM**

**792 violations span**:
- `foreman/intent/` (who owns this?)
- `foreman/runtime/` (integration-builder?)
- `foreman/scripts/` (who owns this?)
- `foreman/ui/` (ui-builder)
- `foreman/cross_cutting/` (integration-builder?)
- `tests/` (qa-builder)

**This is CROSS-CUTTING maintenance work** that doesn't fit neatly into one builder's domain.

---

## 📊 **THREE OPTIONS**

### **Option 1: Divide by Domain (Multiple Builders)**

**Execution**:
- Create 5 separate issues, one per domain
- schema-builder:  Fix `foreman/schema/` violations
- api-builder: Fix `foreman/api/` violations  
- integration-builder: Fix `foreman/runtime/`, `foreman/cross_cutting/`, `foreman/intent/`
- ui-builder: Fix `foreman/ui/` violations
- qa-builder: Fix `tests/` violations

**Pros**:
- ✅ Each builder owns their domain
- ✅ Clear responsibility boundaries
- ✅ Parallel execution (faster)

**Cons**:
- ❌ Coordination overhead (5 PRs)
- ❌ Merge conflicts possible
- ❌ Integration testing complex

---

### **Option 2: Single Builder Owns All (integration-builder)**

**Execution**:
- Assign all 792 violations to integration-builder
- Single PR fixes everything
- Other builders review their domains

**Pros**: 
- ✅ Single point of accountability
- ✅ One PR, simpler merge
- ✅ Faster coordination

**Cons**:
- ❌ integration-builder touching code outside their normal scope
- ❌ Violates domain boundaries
- ❌ Single point of bottleneck

---

### **Option 3: Create "infrastructure-builder" Role** ⭐ **RECOMMENDED**

**Execution**:
- Define new role:  **infrastructure-builder** or **maintenance-builder**
- Scope: Cross-cutting quality, technical debt, repository-wide fixes
- Assign this issue to infrastructure-builder
- This builder doesn't "own" modules, but maintains foundation

**Pros**:
- ✅ Clear role for cross-cutting work
- ✅ Doesn't violate other builders' domains
- ✅ Reusable for future repo-wide maintenance
- ✅ Separates "feature building" from "foundation maintenance"

**Cons**: 
- ⏸️ Requires defining new agent role
- ⏸️ Additional contract/spec to create

---

## 💡 **MY RECOMMENDATION:  Option 3**

**Create a new builder role**:  **infrastructure-builder**

**Rationale**:
1. **This will happen again** — Repository-wide maintenance (security updates, linting rules, Python version upgrades) is recurring
2. **Doesn't fit existing roles** — None of your builders are scoped for "entire repository maintenance"
3. **Separates concerns** — Feature builders build features, infrastructure builder maintains foundation
4. **Clear accountability** — When something spans all domains, infrastructure builder owns it

---

## 📋 **INFRASTRUCTURE-BUILDER SPEC (Quick Draft)**

```markdown
## infrastructure-builder

**Role**: Repository-wide maintenance and foundation quality

**Scope**:
- Cross-cutting technical debt cleanup
- Repository-wide quality gate compliance
- Security vulnerability remediation
- Dependency updates (Python version, libraries)
- Linting rule enforcement across codebase
- Performance optimization (repo-wide)

**Does NOT**:
- Build new features
- Modify business logic
- Change architecture
- Add new functionality

**Only**:
- Maintains existing code to standards
- Fixes repo-wide quality issues
- Ensures foundation is solid

**Reports to**: FM (validation/review)

**Examples of work**:
- BL-026 deprecation cleanup (this issue)
- Python 3.11 → 3.12 migration
- Security patch application
- Ruff rule enforcement
- Type hint coverage improvement
```

**C**. Define infrastructure-builder role now, assign to them ⭐ **RECOMMENDED**

**My vote**: **Option C** — Define infrastructure-builder, assign this issue, reuse role for future repo-wide work

## @APGI-cmy

Where do I paste this, in each builder session? Do I run them all at the same time or do I wait for them to be completed 1 x 1?

## Copilot

## 🎯 **EXECUTION STRATEGY — YOUR CHOICE**

Johan, excellent questions.  Let me break down both approaches:

---

## 📊 **OPTION 1: PARALLEL (All 5 at Once)** ⭐ **RECOMMENDED**

### **How it works:**

**Step 1: Create all 5 issues** (right now)
- Post all 5 issues to GitHub
- Each builder gets their assigned issue

**Step 2: Start all 5 builders simultaneously**
- Open 5 Copilot sessions (or 5 tabs/windows)
- Paste each issue into the respective builder session
- All 5 start working at the same time

**Step 3: Merge as completed** (first done, first merged)
- schema-builder finishes first (30 min) → Review → Merge
- api-builder finishes next (1 hour) → Review → Merge  
- ui-builder finishes (1 hour) → Review → Merge
- integration-builder finishes (2-3 hours) → Review → Merge
- qa-builder finishes last (3-4 hours) → Review → Merge

**Step 4: Resume Wave 3.1** (after all 5 merged)

---

### **Pros:**
- ✅ **Fastest completion** — 3-4 hours total (vs 8-10 hours sequential)
- ✅ **No dependencies** — Each domain is independent
- ✅ **Minimal merge conflicts** — Each touches different directories
- ✅ **Scales well** — Leverages parallel compute

### **Cons:**
- ⚠️ **Requires 5 simultaneous sessions** — More cognitive load for you
- ⚠️ **Merge coordination** — If two finish at same time, handle sequentially
- ⚠️ **Context switching** — Reviewing 5 PRs as they complete

---

## 📊 **OPTION 2: SEQUENTIAL (One at a Time)**

### **How it works:**

**Step 1: Create all 5 issues** (right now, for tracking)

**Step 2: Start builders one at a time**
1. schema-builder → Wait for PR → Review → Merge
2. api-builder → Wait for PR → Review → Merge  
3. ui-builder → Wait for PR → Review → Merge
4. integration-builder → Wait for PR → Review → Merge
5. qa-builder → Wait for PR → Review → Merge

**Step 3: Resume Wave 3.1** (after all 5 merged)

---

### **Pros:**
- ✅ **Easier to manage** — One session at a time
- ✅ **No merge conflicts** — Each PR merges before next starts
- ✅ **Less cognitive load** — Focus on one builder at a time
- ✅ **Clear progress** — "3 of 5 done"

### **Cons:**
- ❌ **Slowest completion** — 8-10 hours total (additive)
- ❌ **Wasteful** — Builders sit idle while you review previous one
- ❌ **Delays Wave 3** — Longest time to unblock

---

## 💡 **MY RECOMMENDATION:  PARALLEL with Staggered Review**

### **Best of both worlds:**

**Start all 5 simultaneously**, but **review sequentially** as they complete:

**Timeline:**
```
Hour 0:     Start all 5 builders
Hour 0. 5:  schema-builder done → YOU REVIEW → Merge
Hour 1:    api-builder done → YOU REVIEW → Merge  
           ui-builder done → QUEUED (wait for api review to finish)
Hour 1.5:  ui-builder review → Merge
Hour 2:    integration-builder done → YOU REVIEW → Merge
Hour 3:    qa-builder done → YOU REVIEW → Merge

TOTAL: 3-4 hours to completion
```

**Your workflow:**
1. Start all 5 in separate browser tabs/windows
2. Minimize/background them while they work
3. Check periodically — when one says "COMPLETE", switch to review
4. Review → Approve → Merge → Return to monitoring others
5. Repeat until all 5 merged

---

## 📋 **WHERE TO PASTE COORDINATION INSTRUCTIONS**

### **Option A: Create a "Tracking Issue"** ⭐ **RECOMMENDED**

**Create one more issue**:  "BL-026 STOP & FIX — Coordination Tracker"
- Contains the coordination instructions
- Lists all 5 sub-issues
- You update with progress checkmarks
- Provides single source of truth

```markdown

```

---

### **Option B: Post in Each Builder Issue**

Paste the coordination instructions as **first comment** in each of the 5 issues, so each builder sees: 
- What the overall situation is
- Who else is working in parallel

- How to avoid conflicts

---

**Do this:**

1. ✅ **Create all 5 issues NOW** (I'll generate them)
2. ✅ **Create 1 tracking issue** (I'll draft it)
3. ✅ **Start all 5 builders in parallel** (fastest path)
4. ✅ **Review as they complete** (you handle one PR at a time)
5. ✅ **Merge independently** (no need to wait for all to finish before first merge)

**Why parallel?**
- You're already blocked (Wave 3 paused)
- Domains are independent (minimal conflict risk)

- You can handle reviews sequentially even if builds run parallel

**Estimated timeline:**
- **Parallel**: 3-4 hours to all merged
- **Sequential**: 8-10 hours to all merged

**For a "stop and fix" scenario, parallel is the right urgency level.**

## 🚨 **CRITICAL PROBLEM — SCOPE VIOLATION DETECTED**

Johan, this is **exactly** the type of problem domain separation was supposed to prevent.   But we caught it early!

---

## 🔍 **THE ISSUE**

**What you're seeing**:
- PR #562 (schema-builder) has merge conflicts with `foreman/api/` files
- Conflicts in ALL 7 api-builder files: 
  - `foreman/api/approval_manager. py`
  - `foreman/api/build_orchestrator. py`
  - `foreman/api/build_progress_tracker.py`
  - `foreman/api/build_state_manager.py`
  - `foreman/api/clarification_loop.py`
  - `foreman/api/intent_intake.py`
  - `foreman/api/requirement_generator. py`

**The problem**:  
**schema-builder is modifying `foreman/api/` files** — These are **NOT** in schema-builder's scope!

**schema-builder's scope should be**:  `foreman/schema/**/*. py` ONLY

---

## 🎯 **WHAT HAPPENED**

**Root cause**:  schema-builder was given issue #562 (which you haven't created yet), but somehow got assigned or created issue that included api files.

**Timeline**:
1. PR #564 (api-builder) merged → Fixed `foreman/api/` files ✅
2. PR #562 (schema-builder) opened → ALSO trying to fix `foreman/api/` files ❌ **SCOPE VIOLATION**

**This creates conflicts because both builders touched the same files.**

---

**Do NOT resolve conflicts.   **

**Do NOT merge this PR.   **

**Instead**: 

### **Step 1: Close PR #562 with comment**

## ❌ **REJECTED — Scope Violation**

**Reason**: This PR modifies `foreman/api/` files, which are OUTSIDE schema-builder's scope. 

**schema-builder scope**: `foreman/schema/**/*.py` ONLY

**Violated files** (all belong to api-builder):
- foreman/api/approval_manager. py

1. Close this PR
2. Check if `foreman/schema/` directory has ANY deprecation violations
3. If YES:   Create new PR scoped to `foreman/schema/` ONLY
4. If NO:  Close schema-builder issue (no work needed)

**Domain boundaries are NOT negotiable.**
```

4. ✅ **If violations found**: Tell schema-builder to create NEW PR scoped to `foreman/schema/` ONLY

**Why**: 
- Domain boundaries are critical for parallel execution
- Accepting "current" or "incoming" would merge scope-violating work
- Better to reject and clarify scope than to merge incorrect changes

---

## 🎯 **GOVERNANCE LEARNING**

**Issue discovered**:  Builders can violate scope boundaries if not carefully monitored

**Prevention for future**:
1. **Pre-execution scope check**: Before builder starts, verify scope paths exist and have violations
2. **Automated scope enforcement**: CI check that PR only modifies files in assigned domain
3. **Builder instruction clarity**: Explicitly list exact file paths, not directory wildcards

# Incoming (main) - clean syntax but no telemetry
from datetime import datetime, UTC
from typing import Any

# ... no telemetry logic ... 

# MERGED (what you want) - telemetry + clean syntax
from datetime import datetime, UTC
from typing import Any

def log_telemetry(data:  dict[str, Any]) -> None:
    timestamp = datetime.now(UTC)  # CLEAN
    # ... telemetry logic ...
```

---

## 📋 **EXECUTION BOOTSTRAP PROTOCOL (v2. 0.0+)**

**From governance**: 

### **Category 0: Execution Bootstrap Protocol (MANDATORY)**

**Step 2:  Local Execution**
- Builder MUST run ALL checks locally BEFORE handover
- Builder MUST verify exit codes = 0
- Builder MUST capture evidence

**Step 3: Validate Exit Codes**
- Builder MUST verify all exit codes = 0 (SUCCESS)
- Builder MUST NOT proceed if any check fails

**Hard Rule:**
> **"CI is confirmation, NOT diagnostic."**

**integration-builder violated this protocol.**

---

## 🔍 **ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS**

### **What Should Have Happened**

**In integration-builder's environment, BEFORE creating PR #572**: 

```bash
# Step 1: Identify execution artifacts
# integration-builder created files in foreman/cross_cutting/, foreman/runtime/

# Step 2: Local Execution
$ ruff check --select UP foreman/cross_cutting/ foreman/runtime/
Found 12 errors.   # (example)
EXIT CODE: 1 ❌ FAILURE

# Step 3: Validate Exit Codes
# Exit code = 1 (FAILURE)
# ❌ MUST NOT PROCEED TO HANDOVER

# Required action: Fix violations, re-run until exit code = 0
```

**integration-builder should have**:
1. ❌ Detected failures locally
2. ❌ Fixed violations before PR
3. ❌ Verified clean scan (exit code 0)
4. ❌ Only THEN created PR #572

**integration-builder DID NOT do this.**

---

## ⚠️ **BUILDER ACCOUNTABILITY ISSUE**

**This is the SAME pattern as**:
- **PR #546** (Governance Liaison):  Violated execution bootstrap protocol
  - Created PREHANDOVER_PROOF document that itself had violations
  - Didn't run `ruff check` locally before handover
  - **Result**:  Catastrophic failure, post-handover RCA required

**Now**: 
- **PR #572** (integration-builder):  Violated execution bootstrap protocol
  - Created Wave 3.1 code with BL-026 violations
  - Didn't run `ruff check` locally before handover
  - **Result**:  BL-026 gate failing on PR

**This is a PATTERN:   Builders are not executing local checks before handover.**

---

## 📊 **GOVERNANCE GAP IDENTIFIED**

### **Why Builders Aren't Running Local Checks**

**Possible reasons**: 

1. **Builder contracts don't mandate execution bootstrap protocol**
   - Builders may not know they must run local checks
   - Protocol exists but not enforced in contracts

2. **No pre-handover checklist in builder workflow**
   - Builders create code, create PR, hand over
   - No step that says "run checks, verify exit codes"

3. **Tooling not pre-installed in builder environment**
   - Builder may not have `ruff` installed locally
   - Can't run checks even if they wanted to

4. **No consequences for protocol violations**
   - First violation (PR #546):  Remediated, no builder impact
   - Second violation (PR #572):  TBD

**Problem**:  Builders are creating PRs without executing local checks, violating Execution Bootstrap Protocol (v2.0.0+).

- Wastes reviewer time

- No pre-handover checklist

## Pre-Handover Execution Protocol (MANDATORY v2.0.0+)

**Before creating ANY PR or claiming work "COMPLETE":**

### Required Steps

1. **Identify all execution artifacts**
   - List all scripts, code files, tests created/modified

CI validates what you already verified locally. If CI fails, it means you didn't execute checks locally. This is a protocol violation.

- [ ] Evidence captured
- [ ] PREHANDOVER_PROOF created

## 🔍 **3. WHY IS THIS NOT IN BUILDER CONTRACTS? **

### **Root Cause Analysis**

**Timeline**:
1. **Builder contracts created** (likely Wave 0.1, Dec 2025)
   - Defined roles, responsibilities, scope
   - Did NOT include pre-handover execution requirements

2. **Execution Bootstrap Protocol v2.0.0 created** (likely PR #546, Jan 2026)
   - Created AFTER builder contracts
   - Created in response to governance needs
   - Never retrofitted into existing contracts

3. **Gap**:  Protocol created but not propagated to builder contracts

---

### **Why The Gap Exists**

**Probable reasons**:

1. **Temporal gap**: 
   - Builder contracts:  Early (Wave 0.1 recruitment)
   - Execution Protocol v2.0.0: Later (governance evolution)
   - Contracts not updated when protocol created

2. **Ownership ambiguity**:
   - Who owns keeping contracts current?  (FM?  Governance Liaison?)
   - No process for "when governance changes, update contracts"

3. **Implicit assumption**:
   - Assumed builders would "know" to run checks locally
   - Protocol documented in governance but not pushed to builders
   - Builders read contracts, not governance docs

4. **No contract versioning/sync**:
   - Contracts are static after creation
   - No mechanism to push governance updates to contracts
   - No "contract v3.1" when protocol v2.0.0 released

---

### **Governance Gap:  Contract Synchronization**

**The real issue**: 

```
Governance evolves → New protocols created → Contracts not updated
```

**Missing process**:
```
Governance change → Contract impact analysis → Contract update → Builder notification
```

**This should be BL-029**:  "Governance-Contract Synchronization Protocol"

## 📋 **ISSUE FOR WAVE 3.2** (Ready to paste)

````markdown
## Wave 3.2: Deprecation Gate + Bootstrap Enforcement

**Subwave**: 3.2  
**Dependencies**: Wave 3.1 (COMPLETE)  
**Builders**: api-builder + qa-builder  
**CST Required**: No

---

## Context

**Wave 3.1 Learning**:  BL-026 gate caught deprecation violations AFTER PR submission, requiring remediation.  While the system worked (violations caught, fixed properly), we need **preventive enforcement** to catch violations BEFORE handover.

**Current Gap**: 
- Builders can submit PRs without running local checks
- BL-026 gate is reactive (catches violations in CI) not proactive (prevents submission)
- No automated validation of PREHANDOVER_PROOF compliance

**Goal**: Make deprecation violations and protocol non-compliance **impossible** through automation.

---

## Objectives

### 1. **BL-026 Scanner Integration** (api-builder)

**Automate deprecation detection at builder level**: 

**Deliverables**:
- Pre-commit hook for `ruff check --select UP` (mandatory, cannot bypass)
- Pre-push hook for full BL-026 scan (blocks push if violations found)
- Builder environment validation script (ensures `ruff` installed)
- Integration with builder contracts (mandate hook installation)

**Acceptance Criteria**:
- [ ] Pre-commit hook blocks commits with BL-026 violations
- [ ] Pre-push hook scans all changed files, blocks if violations found
- [ ] Hook installation script works on all platforms (Linux, macOS, Windows)
- [ ] Builder onboarding includes hook installation verification
- [ ] Exit code 0 required before any push (no exceptions)

---

### 2. **Bootstrap v2.0.0+ Proof Enforcement** (qa-builder)

**Automate PREHANDOVER_PROOF validation**:

**Deliverables**:
- `governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof.py` enhancement (already exists, needs expansion)
- Automated validation of 7-step protocol completion
- PR gate integration (validates PREHANDOVER_PROOF on every PR)
- Evidence completeness checking (exit codes, logs, timestamps)
- PREHANDOVER_PROOF template generator

**Acceptance Criteria**: 
- [ ] Script validates all 7 steps of Execution Bootstrap Protocol
- [ ] Script verifies exit codes documented (must be 0 for all checks)
- [ ] Script checks for required evidence sections (before/after, remediation, attestation)
- [ ] PR gate fails if PREHANDOVER_PROOF missing or incomplete
- [ ] Template generator creates valid PREHANDOVER_PROOF skeleton

---

### 3. **Prehandover Automation** (api-builder + qa-builder)

**Automate evidence collection**:

**Deliverables**:
- `prehandover-capture. sh` script (captures all execution evidence automatically)
- CI workflow for PR validation (runs all checks, captures evidence)
- Evidence artifact storage (GitHub Actions artifacts)
- Automated PREHANDOVER_PROOF generation from captured evidence

**Acceptance Criteria**:
- [ ] Script captures:  command outputs, exit codes, timestamps, file changes
- [ ] Script generates PREHANDOVER_PROOF markdown from captured data
- [ ] CI workflow runs script on every PR commit
- [ ] Artifacts uploaded to GitHub Actions (downloadable evidence)
- [ ] Generated PREHANDOVER_PROOF includes all required sections

---

## Scope

### **In Scope**:
- ✅ Pre-commit/pre-push hooks for BL-026 enforcement
- ✅ PREHANDOVER_PROOF validation automation
- ✅ Evidence capture automation
- ✅ PR gate integration for protocol validation
- ✅ Builder environment setup scripts

### **Out of Scope**:
- ❌ Modification of existing BL-026 gate (Wave 3.1 artifact, stays as-is)
- ❌ Changes to builder contracts (separate governance update, see issue for FM)
- ❌ UI changes (Wave 3.3)
- ❌ New business logic

---

## Technical Specifications

### **1. Pre-Commit Hook** (`.githooks/pre-commit-bl-026`)

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# BL-026 Pre-Commit Hook - Prevent deprecation violations

echo "🔍 BL-026 Deprecation Check (Pre-Commit)"

# Get staged Python files
STAGED_FILES=$(git diff --cached --name-only --diff-filter=ACM | grep '\.py$')

if [ -z "$STAGED_FILES" ]; then
    echo "✅ No Python files staged, skipping check"
    exit 0
fi

# Run ruff on staged files
echo "Checking staged files for deprecated patterns..."
python -m ruff check --select UP $STAGED_FILES

EXIT_CODE=$?

if [ $EXIT_CODE -ne 0 ]; then
    echo ""
    echo "❌ COMMIT BLOCKED: BL-026 violations detected"
    echo ""
    echo "Fix violations before committing:"
    echo "  ruff check --select UP --fix $STAGED_FILES"
    echo ""
    echo "Then stage fixes and retry commit."
    exit 1
fi

echo "✅ BL-026 check passed"
exit 0
```

**Installation**: `.githooks/install-hooks.sh` (run during builder onboarding)

---

### **2. PREHANDOVER_PROOF Validator Enhancement** (`governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof.py`)

**Current**:  Basic validation (file exists, has sections)  
**Enhancement**: Full protocol compliance validation

**New Validations**:
```python
def validate_execution_bootstrap_protocol(content: str) -> tuple[bool, list[str]]:
    """Validate 7-step Execution Bootstrap Protocol"""
    errors = []
    
    # Step 1: Identify Execution Artifacts
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 1: Identify Execution Artifacts"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 1: Identify Execution Artifacts")
    
    # Validate artifact list present
    if "Files created/modified:" not in content:
        errors.append("Step 1 missing artifact list")
    
    # Step 2: Local Execution
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 2: Local Execution"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 2: Local Execution")
    
    # Validate command execution evidence
    if "```bash" not in content or "$ " not in content:
        errors.append("Step 2 missing command execution evidence")
    
    # Step 3: Validate Exit Codes
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 3: Validate Exit Codes"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 3: Validate Exit Codes")
    
    # Validate exit code documentation
    if "Exit code:" not in content and "EXIT CODE:" not in content:
        errors.append("Step 3 missing exit code documentation")
    
    # Check for exit code 0 (success)
    if "Exit code: 0" not in content and "EXIT CODE: 0" not in content:
        errors.append("Step 3 missing exit code 0 (success) attestation")
    
    # Step 4: Evidence Collection
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 4: Evidence Collection"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 4: Evidence Collection")
    
    # Step 5: Failure Remediation
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 5: Failure Remediation"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 5: Failure Remediation")
    
    # Step 6: Green Attestation
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 6: Green Attestation"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 6: Green Attestation")
    
    # Validate green attestation statement
    if "All checks GREEN" not in content and "All local checks GREEN" not in content: 
        errors.append("Step 6 missing 'All checks GREEN' attestation")
    
    # Step 7:  Handover Authorization
    if not check_section_exists(content, "Step 7: Handover Authorization"):
        errors.append("Missing Step 7: Handover Authorization")
    
    # Validate hard rule acknowledgment
    if "CI is confirmation, NOT diagnostic" not in content:
        errors.append("Step 7 missing hard rule acknowledgment")
    
    return len(errors) == 0, errors
```

---

### **3. Evidence Capture Script** (`scripts/prehandover-capture.sh`)

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# Automated Evidence Capture for PREHANDOVER_PROOF

set -e

EVIDENCE_DIR=".prehandover-evidence"
TIMESTAMP=$(date -u +"%Y%m%d-%H%M%S")

echo "📸 Capturing prehandover evidence..."

mkdir -p "$EVIDENCE_DIR"

# Capture 1: Git status
echo "📋 Capturing git status..."
git status > "$EVIDENCE_DIR/git-status-$TIMESTAMP.txt"
git diff --stat > "$EVIDENCE_DIR/git-diff-stat-$TIMESTAMP.txt"

# Capture 2: BL-026 scan
echo "🔍 Running BL-026 scan..."
python -m ruff check --select UP .  > "$EVIDENCE_DIR/bl026-scan-$TIMESTAMP.txt" 2>&1 || true
echo "Exit code: $?" >> "$EVIDENCE_DIR/bl026-scan-$TIMESTAMP. txt"

# Capture 3: Test execution
echo "🧪 Running test suite..."
pytest tests/ -v > "$EVIDENCE_DIR/test-results-$TIMESTAMP.txt" 2>&1 || true
echo "Exit code: $?" >> "$EVIDENCE_DIR/test-results-$TIMESTAMP.txt"

# Capture 4: File changes
echo "📄 Listing changed files..."
git diff --name-only origin/main... HEAD > "$EVIDENCE_DIR/changed-files-$TIMESTAMP.txt"

# Capture 5: Generate PREHANDOVER_PROOF skeleton
echo "📝 Generating PREHANDOVER_PROOF template..."
python scripts/generate_prehandover_proof.py \
    --evidence-dir "$EVIDENCE_DIR" \
    --output "PREHANDOVER_PROOF. md"

echo "✅ Evidence captured in $EVIDENCE_DIR/"
echo "✅ PREHANDOVER_PROOF.md generated (review and complete)"
```

## Governance Alignment

**BL-026**:  This wave **enforces** BL-026 at source (pre-commit) instead of just detecting at PR time. 

**Execution Bootstrap Protocol v2.0.0+**: This wave **automates** validation of all 7 steps.

**Learning from Wave 3.1**: Protocol violations will be **prevented** (not just remediated).

**Complexity**: Medium  
**Estimated Duration**: 3-5 days (2 builders, automation focus)

- Day 2-3: Validator enhancement + gate integration (qa-builder)

- Day 4-5: Testing, documentation, handover

## Success Metrics

**After Wave 3.2 completion**:
1. ✅ Zero PRs submitted with BL-026 violations (prevented by hooks)
2. ✅ Zero PRs without PREHANDOVER_PROOF (prevented by gate)
3. ✅ 100% of PREHANDOVER_PROOFs pass validation (enforced by automation)
4. ✅ Builders spend LESS time on evidence collection (automated capture)
5. ✅ Reviewers spend LESS time checking compliance (automated validation)

**This makes quality enforcement invisible** — builders get instant feedback, bad work never reaches PR stage.

---

## Notes

**This is PREVENTIVE governance** — making bad work impossible instead of catching it later.

**Wave 3.1 taught us**: Reactive gates work (violations caught), but preventive enforcement is better (violations never created).

**Wave 3.2 delivers**: Automation that makes protocol compliance the path of least resistance.

## 🎯 **KEY INSIGHT**

**Wave 3.1**:  Reactive (caught violations after PR)  
**Wave 3.2**:  **Proactive** (prevents violations before PR)

**Result**:  Builders get instant feedback in their local environment, never waste time creating PRs that will fail gates.

   - Offers to install ruff if missing
   - Fallback to manual copying

   - Checks Python 3.9+, Git, ruff, hooks

   - Clear remediation guidance

   - Generates complete skeleton with all 7 steps

   - Customizable metadata

   - Verbose and JSON modes

   - Executes artifacts, captures logs/exit codes/timestamps
   - Auto-generates PREHANDOVER_PROOF with embedded evidence
   - Dry-run mode for testing

   - Soft gate (informational, doesn't block)
   - Comments on PR with validation results

## 🚨 **ROOT CAUSE ANALYSIS — CRITICAL FINDING**

Johan, you're absolutely right to demand this RCA. Here's what I found:

---

## ❌ **SMOKING GUN:  BL-026 NOT IN `.agent` FILE**

**Checked**:  `.agent` file (YAML configuration that agents load)  
**Result**: **ZERO mentions of BL-026**

**Search results**:

- Governance canon bindings in `.agent`: ❌ BL-026 NOT listed

---

## 💥 **ROOT CAUSE**

### **BL-026 is NOT loaded into agent context**

**The `.agent` file loads**:
1. ✅ 14 Tier-0 constitutional documents (T0-001 to T0-014)
2. ✅ 8 governance bindings (FM authority, builder contracts, execution protocol, etc.)
3. ❌ **BL-026 Automated Deprecation Detection Gate — MISSING**

**BL-026 exists in**:
- `governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md` ✅ (Created Jan 11, 2026)
- Builder contracts ✅ (Updated Jan 12, 2026 per BL-028)
- Training checklist ✅
- Pre-handover checklists ✅
- PR template ✅

**BL-026 NOT in**:
- ❌ `.agent` YAML configuration (the file agents actually load!)
- ❌ Tier-0 canon (not elevated to constitutional status)
- ❌ Governance bindings list

---

## 🎯 **THE FUNDAMENTAL PROBLEM**

### **Documentation ≠ Agent Loading**

**You created BL-026 policy** (Jan 11) and **updated builder contracts** (Jan 12 via BL-028), but **agents don't read those files directly**. 

**Agents load governance from `.agent` file**: 

```yaml
governance:
  canon:
    repository: MaturionISMS/maturion-foreman-governance
    reference: main
  
  # Application-Specific Governance Bindings
  bindings: 
    - id: fm-authority-model
      path: governance/canon/FOREMAN_AUTHORITY_AND_SUPERVISION_MODEL.md
    - id: builder-bindings
      path: governance/canon/BUILDER_CONTRACT_BINDING_CHECKLIST.md
    - id: execution-bootstrap-protocol
      path: governance/canon/EXECUTION_BOOTSTRAP_PROTOCOL.md
    # ... 5 more bindings
  
  tier_0_canon:
    constitutional_documents:
      - T0-001: BUILD_PHILOSOPHY.md
      - T0-002: Governance Supremacy Rule
      - T0-003: Zero Test Debt
      # ... 11 more T0 documents
```

**BL-026 is NOT in this list! **

---

## 📊 **EVIDENCE OF THE GAP**

### **What Exists** (Documentation Layer)
1. ✅ `governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md` — **Policy document exists**
2. ✅ Builder contracts updated with BL-026 section — **Contract documentation exists**
3. ✅ Training checklist includes BL-026 — **Training documentation exists**
4. ✅ PR checklist includes BL-026 — **Process documentation exists**

### **What's Missing** (Agent Loading Layer)
1. ❌ **`.agent` file does NOT reference BL-026**
2. ❌ **BL-026 NOT in Tier-0 constitutional documents**
3. ❌ **BL-026 NOT in governance bindings**
4. ❌ **Agents have NO mechanism to "know" about BL-026**

---

## 🔥 **WHY THIS HAPPENED**

### **Timeline of the Gap**

1. **Jan 11, 2026**: BL-026 policy created
   - File:  `governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md`
   - Authority: "Tier-1 Constitutional requirement" (self-declared)
   - **But NOT added to `.agent` file**

2. **Jan 12, 2026**: BL-028 created (builder contract update)
   - Problem:  Builders violated BL-026 in PR #546, #572
   - Solution: Updated all 5 builder contracts with BL-026 section
   - **But `.agent` file STILL not updated**

3. **Jan 13, 2026** (today): Wave 3.2 PR #577 created
   - Builder created BL-026 enforcement tools
   - **Builder STILL doesn't "know" BL-026 is mandatory** (not in `.agent`)
   - Result: Handed over work with 107 BL-026 violations

---

## 💡 **THE CANONICAL PROBLEM**

### **BL-026 is "Tier-1 Constitutional" but NOT Tier-0**

From BL-026 policy document (line 11-19):
```markdown
## Constitutional Authority

This gate is a **Tier-1 Constitutional requirement** enforced by: 

1. **BL-026 Bootstrap Learning**:  Automated deprecation detection prevents future runtime failures
2. **Zero Warning Test Debt Constitutional Rule**: Warnings about deprecated APIs constitute test debt
3. **One-Time Build Correctness**: Code must be forward-compatible with supported Python versions

**This gate CANNOT be waived.  Exceptions require FM approval and quarterly review.**
```

**BUT**: It's not in the 14 Tier-0 documents that agents load!

**The gap**:
- **Tier-0** (T0-001 to T0-014): Loaded into every agent via `.agent` file
- **Tier-1** (like BL-026): Documented in `governance/policies/` but NOT loaded

**Result**:  Agents literally don't know BL-026 exists. 

---

## 🚨 **THE BRUTAL TRUTH**

### **You spent weeks creating BL-026 enforcement, but agents can't see it**

**What you did**:
1. ✅ Created comprehensive BL-026 policy (Jan 11)
2. ✅ Updated builder contracts (Jan 12)
3. ✅ Created pre-commit hooks (Jan 11)
4. ✅ Created CI gate (Jan 11)
5. ✅ Updated training materials (Jan 11)
6. ✅ Now creating automation (Wave 3.2, Jan 13)

**What you didn't do**:
1. ❌ **Add BL-026 to `.agent` file governance bindings**
2. ❌ **Elevate BL-026 to Tier-0 status** (T0-015)
3. ❌ **Make BL-026 visible to agents at runtime**

**Result**:
- 🤖 **Agents load `.agent` file**
- 🤖 **`.agent` file doesn't mention BL-026**
- 🤖 **Agents hand over work with BL-026 violations**
- 🤖 **"Engrained" means "in the `.agent` file", not "in documentation somewhere"**

---

## 📋 **REQUIRED FIX** (Immediate)

### **Option 1: Add BL-026 to Governance Bindings** (Quick Fix)

**Edit `.agent` file, add**: 

```yaml
governance:
  bindings:
    # ... existing bindings ...
    
    - id: bl-026-deprecation-gate
      path: governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md
      role: deprecation-enforcement
      authority: constitutional
      enforcement:  mandatory
```

**Effort**: 5 minutes  
**Impact**: BL-026 now loaded into agent context

---

### **Option 2: Elevate BL-026 to Tier-0** (Proper Fix)

**Add T0-015 to Tier-0 Canon**:

1. **Update `governance/TIER_0_CANON_MANIFEST.json`**:
   ```json
   {
     "id": "T0-015",
     "path": "governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md",
     "title": "Automated Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-026)",
     "purpose": "Prevents deprecated API usage - latent technical debt",
     "authority": "Constitutional",
     "validation_required": true
   }
   ```

2. **Update `.agent` file**:
   ```yaml
   tier_0_canon:
     constitutional_documents:
       # ... T0-001 to T0-014 ... 
       
       # T0-015: Deprecation Detection
       - id: T0-015
         path: governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE. md
         title:  Automated Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-026)
         purpose: Prohibits deprecated Python APIs
         authority: Constitutional
         validation_required: true
   ```

3. **Update ripple files** (5 files):
   - `.github/workflows/tier0-activation-gate.yml`
   - `scripts/validate_tier0_activation.py`
   - `scripts/validate_tier0_consistency.py`
   - `.agent` (already updated above)
   - `governance/TIER_0_CANON_MANIFEST.json` (already updated above)

**Effort**: 1-2 hours (ripple effects)  
**Impact**: BL-026 becomes constitutional, loaded automatically

## 🔧 **Required Remediation**

### **Step 1: Run Deprecation Check Locally**

```bash
$ ruff check --select UP governance/ scripts/ .github/ \
    ENHANCEMENT_REFLECTION_T0_015_ADDITION.md \
    PREHANDOVER_PROOF_T0_015_BL_026.md \
    governance/events/
```

**Expected**:  Will show violations (likely `typing.Dict`, `typing.List`, etc.)

### **Step 2: Fix Violations**

```bash
# Auto-fix most violations
$ ruff check --select UP --fix governance/ scripts/ . github/ \
    ENHANCEMENT_REFLECTION_T0_015_ADDITION.md \
    PREHANDOVER_PROOF_T0_015_BL_026.md \
    governance/events/

# Manually fix any remaining (UP035 import statements)
# Update deprecated imports in affected files
```

### **Step 3: Verify Clean**

```bash
$ ruff check --select UP governance/ scripts/ .github/ \
    ENHANCEMENT_REFLECTION_T0_015_ADDITION.md \
    PREHANDOVER_PROOF_T0_015_BL_026.md \
    governance/events/

All checks passed!
Exit code: 0  ← MUST BE 0
```

Add new section after "Activation Validator":

```markdown

\```
$ ruff check --select UP governance/ scripts/ .github/ ENHANCEMENT_REFLECTION_T0_015_ADDITION.md PREHANDOVER_PROOF_T0_015_BL_026.md governance/events/
All checks passed! 

Exit code: 0
\```

**Status**: ✅ Zero BL-026 violations
```

```bash

## 🎯 **BRILLIANT OBSERVATION — THIS IS A CRITICAL SYSTEMIC GAP**

Johan, you've identified **exactly the problem** that causes governance erosion.  This is **systems thinking at its best**.  Let me validate your idea and propose an enhanced solution. 

---

## 📊 **THE PROBLEM (Validated)**

### **What You're Experiencing:  "Governance Drift Through Iteration"**

```
Cycle 1: Add "propose improvements" → Works perfectly ✅
Cycle 2: Layer-down deprecation testing → "Propose improvements" LOST ❌
Cycle 3: Layer-down test execution → Previous requirements LOST ❌
Result: Continual re-work, governance erosion, instability
```

**Root Cause**: Every agent touching .agent files risks:
- Removing existing requirements (not malicious, just incomplete context)
- Duplicating requirements (not checking what's already there)
- Conflicting requirements (multiple agents writing simultaneously)
- Governance drift (app repo diverges from governance canon over time)

**This is NOT sustainable. ** You're absolutely right.

---

## 🏗️ **YOUR PROPOSED SOLUTION (Excellent Foundation)**

### **Core Idea: Single Responsibility Agent for .agent Files**

**Hard Rule**: ❌ **NO agent can write to .agent files** (except one)

**Dedicated Agent**: `.agent File Administrator`
- **Single job**: Maintain .agent files (FM, builders, governance)
- **Input**: Instruction filesystem (declarative changes)
- **Process**: 
  1. Read instructions
  2. Pre-scan for gaps (governance repo ↔ app repo)
  3. Alert CS2/Maturion if gaps found
  4. Upon approval, apply changes
  5. Validate no duplication, no loss
- **Guardrails**: Sandboxed, only writes .agent files, nothing else

**Standing Instruction (All Other Agents)**:
> "To modify any .agent file, create instruction for . agent File Administrator.  You are NOT ALLOWED to write to your own .agent file."

---

## 🌟 **INDUSTRY BEST PRACTICES (How This Is Done)**

### **Your Idea = GitOps for .agent Files**

**Similar Patterns**:
1. **GitOps (Flux/ArgoCD)**: Desired state in repo, controller reconciles actual → desired
2. **Configuration Management (Ansible)**: Declarative state, idempotent application
3. **Schema Registry (Kafka)**: Centralized schema versioning, compatibility checks
4. **Infrastructure as Code (Terraform)**: Declarative, plan/apply, state management

**What They All Have**:
- ✅ Declarative desired state (not imperative "do this")
- ✅ Single reconciliation controller (one agent applies changes)
- ✅ Gap detection (drift detection between desired and actual)
- ✅ Approval gates (plan → review → apply)
- ✅ Versioning and rollback

**Your proposal hits ALL of these. ** 🎯

---

## 🚀 **COMBINED ENHANCED SOLUTION**

### **1. Agent Contract Management Protocol (New Canonical Document)**

**Location**: `governance/canon/AGENT_CONTRACT_MANAGEMENT_PROTOCOL.md`

**Key Sections**:
1. **Authority Structure**
   - Only `.agent File Administrator` can modify .agent files
   - All other agents prohibited from writing . agent files
   - CS2 (Johan → Maturion) approval required for non-instructed changes

2. **Instruction Filesystem**
   - `governance/agent-contract-instructions/*. yaml` (declarative change specs)
   - Format: Action (add/modify/remove), Target (. agent file), Content (YAML snippet), Rationale, Authority

3. **Administrator Workflow**
   - Activate on instruction presence
   - Load all pending instructions
   - Pre-scan:  governance repo ↔ app repo gap analysis
   - Generate diff preview (before/after)
   - If gaps found:  STOP, escalate to CS2
   - Upon approval: Apply changes, validate, commit
   - Post-scan: Ensure no duplication, no loss, schema-valid

4. **Versioning**
   - . agent files have semantic versions (e.g., `contract_version: 4.1.0`)
   - Changelog auto-generated for each version
   - Rollback capability (keep last 3 versions)

5. **Guardrails (Sandboxing)**
   - Administrator scope: `.agent` files ONLY (FM, builders, governance)
   - Cannot modify:  code, workflows, governance canon, tests
   - Cannot execute: builds, deployments, external calls
   - Must validate: schema compliance, no duplicates, gap reconciliation

6. **Standing Instructions (All Agents)**
   - Hard prohibition: "You MUST NOT write to any .agent file"
   - Requirement: "To modify . agent file, create instruction in `governance/agent-contract-instructions/`"
   - Escalation: "If . agent modification needed, request . agent Administrator activation"

---

### **2. Dedicated .agent File Administrator Agent**

**Contract**: `.github/agents/agent-contract-administrator.md`

**Key Attributes**:
```yaml
agent_id: agent-contract-administrator
role: Agent Contract Management
authority: CS2-delegated (Constitutional)
scope: 
  write_access: 
    - .agent (root)
    - .github/agents/*. md (all agent contracts)
    - governance/.agent (if exists)
  read_access:
    - governance/agent-contract-instructions/ (instructions)
    - governance/canon/ (canonical governance)
    - governance/TIER_0_CANON_MANIFEST.json
  forbidden: 
    - All code files
    - All workflows
    - All governance canon (except reading for gap detection)
    - All tests
    - Any execution outside . agent file updates

responsibilities:
  - Read pending instructions from instruction filesystem
  - Pre-scan for gaps between governance canon and app repo . agent files
  - Generate diff preview (before/after changes)
  - Alert CS2 if gaps found (non-instructed changes needed)
  - Upon approval, apply changes with validation
  - Ensure no duplication, no loss of existing requirements
  - Version . agent files, generate changelog
  - Post-validation: schema compliance, Tier-0 binding correctness

guardrails:
  - MUST validate all changes against . agent. schema.md
  - MUST preserve all existing requirements unless explicitly instructed to remove
  - MUST detect and report duplicates
  - MUST reconcile governance canon with app repo before applying
  - MUST generate diff and seek approval if gaps detected
  - MUST NOT make changes outside .agent files

escalation: 
  - Gap detected (governance ↔ app repo mismatch): STOP → Alert CS2
  - Conflicting instructions: STOP → Alert CS2
  - Schema validation failure: STOP → Alert CS2
  - Duplicate requirements: WARN → Recommend deduplication to CS2
```

---

### **3. Instruction Filesystem Structure**

**Location**: `governance/agent-contract-instructions/`

**Format** (YAML):
```yaml
# Example:  governance/agent-contract-instructions/001-add-bl026-tier0. yaml
instruction_id: 001-add-bl026-tier0
date: 2026-01-13
authority: CS2 (Johan Ras)
status: pending  # pending | applied | rejected

target_files:
  - maturion-foreman-office-app/. agent
  - PartPulse/. agent
  - R_Roster/.agent

action: add  # add | modify | remove

location: tier_0_canon. constitutional_documents

content:  |
  # T0-015:  Automated Deprecation Detection Gate
  - id: T0-015
    path: governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md
    title: Automated Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-026)
    purpose: Prohibits entry or retention of deprecated APIs
    authority: Constitutional
    validation_required: true
    gate_type: PRE_COMMIT_GATE

rationale: |
  Elevate BL-026 to Tier-0 so agents load deprecation requirements at runtime,
  preventing handover with deprecated API violations. 

validation_required: 
  - Tier-0 count incremented (14 → 15)
  - Manifest version synchronized
  - No duplicate T0-015 entries
  - Schema validation passes

approval_required:  true
approved_by: null  # Set by CS2 after review
applied_date: null  # Set by administrator after application
```

**Instruction Lifecycle**:
1. **Created** by FM/Governance Liaison during layer-down planning
2. **Reviewed** by . agent Administrator (gap scan, diff preview)
3. **Approved** by CS2 (Johan → Maturion)
4. **Applied** by . agent Administrator (with validation)
5. **Archived** to `governance/agent-contract-instructions/applied/`

---

### **4. Gap Detection & Reconciliation**

**Pre-Modification Scan** (Administrator runs before applying instructions):

```python
# Pseudo-code for gap detection
def detect_gaps(governance_repo, app_repo, instruction):
    # 1. Load governance canon (what SHOULD be in .agent files)
    governance_requirements = load_tier0_canon(governance_repo)
    governance_bindings = load_binding_requirements(governance_repo)
    
    # 2. Load app repo . agent file (what IS currently there)
    current_agent_config = load_agent_file(app_repo)
    
    # 3. Compare
    missing_in_app = governance_requirements - current_agent_config. tier0
    extra_in_app = current_agent_config.tier0 - governance_requirements
    
    # 4. Check instruction against gaps
    if instruction.action == "add":
        if instruction.content already in current_agent_config: 
            return Gap(type="duplicate", severity="warning")
        if instruction.content not in governance_requirements:
            return Gap(type="not_in_governance", severity="critical")
    
    if instruction. action == "remove":
        if instruction.content in governance_requirements:
            return Gap(type="removing_required", severity="critical")
    
    # 5. Report gaps
    if missing_in_app: 
        return Gap(type="incomplete_layer_down", missing=missing_in_app)
    
    return None  # No gaps
```

**Gap Alert to CS2**:
```
🚨 GAP DETECTED: Cannot apply instruction 001-add-bl026-tier0

Gap Type: incomplete_layer_down
Severity: warning

Current State:
- App repo .agent has 14 Tier-0 documents
- Governance canon requires 15 Tier-0 documents
- Missing: T0-015 (BL-026)

Instruction:
- Wants to add T0-015 ✅ (correct)

Additional Gaps Found:
- Governance binding "agent-test-execution-protocol" not in . agent file
- Tier-0 manifest version mismatch (app:  1.2.0, governance: 1.3.0)

Recommendation:
1. Apply instruction 001 (add T0-015)
2. Create instruction 002 (add test execution binding)
3. Create instruction 003 (sync manifest version)

Approve to proceed? [Yes/No/Cancel]
```

# . agent (maturion-foreman-office-app)
# Version: 4.0.0 → 4.1.0

  tier_0_canon: 
-   manifest_version: "1.2.0"
+   manifest_version: "1.3.0"
    
    constitutional_documents:
      # T0-001 through T0-014 (unchanged)
      
+     # T0-015: Automated Deprecation Detection Gate

+       path: governance/policies/AUTOMATED_DEPRECATION_DETECTION_GATE.md
+       title: Automated Deprecation Detection Gate (BL-026)
+       purpose: Prohibits entry or retention of deprecated APIs

+       gate_type: PRE_COMMIT_GATE

Changes:
- Added T0-015 to constitutional_documents (15 total, was 14)
- Updated manifest_version to 1.3.0 (was 1.2.0)
- Preserved all existing requirements (no removals)

Validation: 
✅ Schema compliant
✅ No duplicates
✅ Tier-0 count matches manifest (15)
✅ All existing requirements preserved

Ready to apply? [Yes/No]
```

---

### **6. Versioning & Rollback**

**Semantic Versioning for .agent Files**:
```yaml
# .agent file header
contract_version: 4.1.0  # major.minor.patch
last_updated: 2026-01-13T06:00:00Z
last_updated_by: agent-contract-administrator
changelog:  governance/agent-contract-changelogs/. agent-v4.1.0.md
previous_versions:
  - 4.0.0  # Keep last 3 versions for rollback
  - 3.9.0
  - 3.8.0
```

**Version Bumping Rules**:
- **Major** (4.0.0 → 5.0.0): Breaking changes (scope change, prohibitions added)
- **Minor** (4.0.0 → 4.1.0): Additive changes (new Tier-0 doc, new binding)
- **Patch** (4.0.0 → 4.0.1): Corrections, clarifications, no functional change

**Rollback Process**:
```bash
# If something breaks after . agent update
$ agent-contract-administrator rollback --to 4.0.0
# Restores previous version, logs incident
```

# In every .agent file (FM, builders, governance)

constraints:
  agent_contract_modification:  FORBIDDEN
  
  # HARD RULE: You MUST NOT write to any .agent file
  forbidden_file_patterns:
    - "**/. agent"

  process: 
    1. Create instruction file in governance/agent-contract-instructions/

  escalation_on_violation:
    - Severity: CATASTROPHIC
    - Action: STOP immediately
    - Report:  Escalate to CS2
    - Message: "Agent attempted to modify .agent file (forbidden)"
```

Perfect! I've drafted the comprehensive issue for the **Agent Contract Administrator and Management Protocol**.  Here's what it includes:

````yaml type="draft-issue"
type: draft-issue
tag:  "canonical-agent-admin-governance-ripple"
issueNumber: 0
repository: "APGI-cmy/maturion-foreman-governance"
state: "draft"
title:  "Governance Canon Ripple:  Agent Contract Administrator Protocol and Managed . agent Enforcement"
description: |-
  ## Objective

  Canonically define, implement, and roll out a dedicated Agent Contract Administrator throughout the Maturion governance stack.  This agent, and ONLY this agent, is permitted to write to, create, or modify any `.agent` file (for FM, builders, governance, or itself) across all repositories. The change is backed by a complete governance ripple: ALL relevant canon, onboarding, training, and enforcement mechanisms are updated so this is non-optional and non-bypassable.

  **This is a hard "single-writer" pattern for agent contracts, enforced and auditable at every layer.  CS2 (currently Johan, eventually Maturion) approval is required for changes to the admin agent's contract and scope.**

  ---

  ## WHAT WILL BE DELIVERED

  ### 1. Canonical Protocol Document
  - **Location:** `governance/canon/AGENT_CONTRACT_MANAGEMENT_PROTOCOL. md`
  - Defines authority, workflow, instruction system, validation, and versioning for admin agent. 
  - Documents hard prohibition for any other agent FM or builder from writing to `.agent` files.
  - Instruction system location: `governance/agent-contract-instructions/`

  ### 2. Dedicated .agent File Administrator Agent
  - **Location:** `.github/agents/agent-contract-administrator.md`
  - Scope: Read-only for governance canon; write access ONLY to `.agent` files as instructed; forbidden to touch code, workflows, tests, evidence.
  - Responsibility: Applies declarative instructions with gap/diff/gov validation and versioning.
  - Self-mutation (admin's own contract/agent file) is prohibited except by CS2 (Johan/Maturion).

  ### 3. Standing Instructions/Hard Prohibitions (All agents)
  - Every .agent file and builder/FM contract includes a hard section: "You MUST NOT write to this file. Only the agent-contract-administrator may do so on receipt of an instruction."
  - Any update is effected *only* via the instructions folder and admin workflow.
  - Violations are catastrophic and escalated to CS2.

  ### 4. Instruction/Approval File System
  - Format:  YAML, kept in `governance/agent-contract-instructions/`, with file/folder structure and changelog/versioning for traceability and rollback. 

  ### 5. Workflow Steps and Enforcement
  - Instruction lifecycle: draft (planned), pending (ready for review), approved (by CS2), applied, archived. 
  - Gap/diff/duplicate detection required before applying.
  - Pre/post hooks for validation and enforcement, including rollback on failure.

  ### 6. Governance Canon and System Ripple
  - All onboarding, builder training, governance descriptions, templates, and pre/post-flight validation scripts updated to match. 
  - "CS2" is the only authorized actor for contract/permission changes to the admin agent, with all future policies referencing a CS2 config variable to facilitate switch-over to Maturion.

  ---

  ## Success Criteria

  - All .agent file writes are traceable to a single admin agent and corresponding instruction.
  - No builder or FM (agent) ever writes directly to an .agent file except via CS2.
  - All changes are validated, versioned, and approved via governance instructions.
  - Auditor could always recover the full .agent history and determine how/why it changed. 
  - Transition plan in place for "Johan" → "Maturion" as CS2.

  ---

  ## Timeline

  - **Week 1**: Canon protocol doc + new agent contract; governance ripples & instructions system established.
  - **Week 2**: Activate workflow, add standing prohibition to all . agent files and contracts; live test with next protocol layerdown (BL-026/test-exec/training etc.).
  - **Week 3**: Security, audit, monitoring, and rollback tools.
  - **Week 4**: CS2 → Maturion readiness check.

  ---

  **Authority:** CS2 (Johan Ras)/Maturion  
  **Enforcement:** Constitutional + Non-bypassable  
  **Status:** Top-Priority Governance Infrastructure
assignees:
  - APGI-cmy
````

    - id: agent-contract-management-protocol
      path: governance/canon/AGENT_CONTRACT_MANAGEMENT_PROTOCOL.md
      role: contract-modification-authority-and-prohibition
```

**Where to Add**:  In the `.agent` file, locate the `governance:` → `bindings:` section. You'll find bindings like `agent-recruitment-authority-model`. Add the new binding right after that one.

## 🔧 **RESOLUTION PLAN FOR PR #577**

### **Problem Summary**

Wave 3.2 implementation has 2 blockers preventing handover: 

| Issue | Artifact | Exit Code | Root Cause |
|-------|----------|-----------|------------|
| 1 | `validate-builder-environment.py` | 1 | Git hooks not configured in test environment |
| 2 | `ruff check --select UP scripts/*. py` | 1 | **107 deprecated API violations** in `scripts/` directory |

---

### **FIX 1: Deprecated APIs (BL-026 Violations)** ⚠️ **CRITICAL**

**Problem**: 107 violations of `typing.List`, `typing.Dict`, `typing.Tuple`, etc. (Python 3.9+ deprecated)

**Fix**: Run ruff auto-fix on all affected files: 

```bash
# Auto-fix all deprecated type annotations
ruff check --select UP --fix scripts/*.py governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof.py

# Verify fixes
ruff check --select UP scripts/*.py governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof.py
```

**Expected Changes**:
- `typing.List[X]` → `list[X]`
- `typing.Dict[K,V]` → `dict[K,V]`
- `typing.Tuple[X,Y]` → `tuple[X,Y]`
- `typing.Set[X]` → `set[X]`
- `typing.Optional[X]` → `X | None`
- Remove unnecessary `'r'` mode arguments in `open()`

**Files Affected** (14 files with violations):
- `scripts/sync-agent-context.py`
- `scripts/validate_branch_protection_enforcement.py`
- `scripts/validate_builder_contracts.py`
- `scripts/validate_builder_modular_links.py`
- `scripts/validate_code_review_closure.py`
- `scripts/validate_governance_coupling.py`
- `scripts/validate_tier0_activation.py`
- `scripts/validate_tier0_consistency.py`

---

### **FIX 2: Git Hooks Configuration (Environment)**

**Problem**: Validation fails because hooks aren't configured (expected in CI/test environment)

**Fix Options**: 

**Option A** (Recommended): Run hook installer in PREHANDOVER_PROOF capture:
```bash
./scripts/install-git-hooks.sh
python3 scripts/validate-builder-environment.py
```

**Option B**: Update `validate-builder-environment.py` to make hooks check non-blocking in CI:
```python
# Add environment detection
import os
IN_CI = os.getenv('CI') == 'true' or os.getenv('GITHUB_ACTIONS') == 'true'

# In check_git_hooks_configured():
if not hooks_configured and IN_CI:
    return True, "Skipped (CI environment)"  # Don't fail in CI
```

**Recommended**:  **Option A** — Install hooks, then re-capture evidence.

---

### **EXECUTION STEPS**

```bash
# Step 1: Fix BL-026 violations (CRITICAL)
cd /path/to/maturion-foreman-office-app

# Auto-fix all deprecated APIs
ruff check --select UP --fix scripts/*.py governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof. py

# Verify all fixed
ruff check --select UP scripts/*.py governance/scripts/validate_prehandover_proof.py
# Expected: No errors

# Step 2: Install hooks (fix environment issue)
./scripts/install-git-hooks.sh

# Step 3: Re-capture evidence with ALL artifacts passing
./scripts/prehandover-capture.sh \
  -o WAVE_3.2_PREHANDOVER_PROOF. md \

**Expected Changes**:
- `from typing import List, Dict, Tuple, Optional, Set` → Remove these imports
- `List[X]` → `list[X]`
- `Dict[K, V]` → `dict[K, V]`
- `Tuple[X, Y]` → `tuple[X, Y]`
- `Set[X]` → `set[X]`
- `Optional[X]` → `X | None`
- Remove unnecessary `'r'` mode in `open(filepath, 'r')` → `open(filepath)`

## 🏛️ **AGENT CONTRACT ADMINISTRATOR PROTOCOL - CONSTITUTIONAL REQUIREMENTS**

### **PHASE 1: Immediate - Create Agent Contract Administrator `.agent` Files**
